The treatment of wounds is according to this form: and it is that you convert the parchment and make it inside according to what I have said, and then make .ij. wounds by art, and .ij. subtle threads as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula is; and take .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above the surface of the parchment of the eye, and stretch the .ij. threads of the .ij. parties firmly; and leave them thus for some days, and the skin that was stretched will mortify and putrefy and decay, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the wound has united forces, then cure it so that it may be healthy; and when the wound is cicatrized, and if the paper is lifted, and they do not prick the hairs anymore; and this is the form of the twelve canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a subtle needle, and thread a soft and subtle silk thread; then assemble the heads and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the hunt another subtle silk thread briefly, and tie the head of the two threads; then put the patient's head in your healthy place; and let it be in the shade if possible, so that the works are declared, for it is a subtle and minor work, then put the needle in all the hunt at the root of the hair opposite, and make it pierce into the paper hastily as much as you can pull it out above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the hunt, and put one of those hairs in the hunt, if there is one or two or three or more; then extract your hand so that the hairs come out at all the hunt on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the hunt down to all the thread that you had ordered there, so that the hunt comes out of the hole above and that you see it by the vision of the eye; then pull the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and let it be closed for twelve hours or thirteen, until the hair is rooted in its place and grows the flesh above; and if the hairs are small, then accompany one long hair of natural whiskers, and elevate it with that which you leave, so that it may be elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rotting of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the rotting of the eye occurs, it happens in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a cut, or from cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of working on it is that you split open the suture, and separate the lips of it, and put in thread of linen, and lay it so it may be healthy; and it does not seem to use in its cure things that dry and constrict. For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but it works with mollifying things, such as fenugreic; and the rose water or alembroth and linseed oil are cooked, and ointments of dyapulum founded on none of the eyes, and it envelops a tent, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take heed so it does not swell according to its former shape; and these workings that we have spoken of are only remedies for this disease, so it does not return according to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is beneath and truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wounds and fractures and cautery and similar things; and the way of working on it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and prick the flesh, and make the left arm's vein bleed so much to the right, so that the threads join at the head of the flesh; then place the flesh above all the needle, and cover with a large spatulum.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the papyrus returns according to what is convenient, it's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the wound, and turn the papyrus, and make two wounds or cuts within the papyrus; and be the heads of the two wounds at the angles of the incision that you have covered, and be made into an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter that has no "griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity whose edges are cut beneath, from what follows the papyrus, then add the two separated parts, and sew with a thread of wool; then cure with what we have said about mollifying medicines and tents, until it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or cut or cautery, it is convenient that you make a plain wound beneath the hairs of the papyrus, and according to what is before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know how to make the figure return to its natural form; and the same diseases, according to what is convenient for treatment and more dispositional remedies.
dou soudement de la papiere	you should cauterize with a paper instrument
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this cauterization has its effect on men in such a way that the paper above is sodden with the white of the oil, and cannot move or perform their natural functions, then it is necessary to put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it high; and hold as pincers, until you grasp what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient may not suffer from the spatula being too sharp or bleeding the oil; and make your incision, where you gently scrape off the assembled parts, lightly, so that the paper regains its natural shape; and it is all healthy, and there are no more frequent problems in the oily area, and the lifted watery discharge, and of the collar; then put between the paper and oil a linen thread, and put on the oil a moistened cloth in abundance of egg whites; and after three days use sweet collars and soothing things until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It knows that the corner of the eye is in two ways: it is nervous and similar to a hard crust, and another which is not nervous but seems like a white moist congealed moisture, that when you touch it with iron and pinch it with pincers, it cannot be removed; and one and the other have a similar effect towards the large artery, and gradually increase until it covers all vision and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Here is the translation:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware that the scalpel does not touch the tender skin and break it, and that the pruning is not perceived; and after the incision pour a little of the bruised oil into the eye, and make a dressing with litarge, and leave it until the next day; then cure what needs to be cured so that it may be healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the uncines cannot enter, many times it is cured with a similar type of nail medicine; and grows as I have related in the division, and if you see it covered, if you open the eye of the patient, and take the scalpel lightly a little agitated according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail subtly, and if you see that it diminishes little by little and the reason appears, then distill from your mouth into the eye a dressing made of litarge and red ochre and bruised oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then recommence the other treatment according to this same method of opening, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, as if an abscess forms, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess so that it may be healthy, then recommence the treatment as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh is damaged by the armorer's night in the eye through great nuisance, if it suspends from the onion, and in coping with one part and not all, that the course of tears does not come; then distill in the eye a reddish-colored collyrium made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the knee
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Their eyes grow red like a rose of baluster, and cover the knee and restrain it with bandages and turn to the doctor, and seem; and the work is that the patient puts his head in his healthy state, then opens his eyes, and gathers all that flesh as uncines convenient to that, and supports it with force; then copes the first flesh, and goes entirely to the raspator until the end, and guards that no blepharitis affects the eye at the work; and is the incision of the spatula which we have said in the incision of the ankle and small forces of what one esteems, just as the form appears after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then anoint the eye with a broiet or distill a reddish-colored collyrium and apply medicines corrosives, and put on the eye a cotton with egg white, so that it may be assured of a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the wound begins to suppurate, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye and cure the abscess with soothing things that calm the hot abscess; then return to your work as long as it is healthy, and thus make all the characters that are adjusted in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in any case it is necessary that you lift the treatment of each oil from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in work with iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that are covered over the eye, and they obstruct the sight with their work and weaken the eye for many years. Therefore it is necessary at first that you examine if the eye is in this state, whether it is strong or not, and there is no other illness beyond the vein; then you should coil it in such a manner: instruct the patient to put his head in a healthy position, then suspend those veins all around according to their wisdom, and let the subtle double veins be according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the vein be divided into degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one coils the subtle forces of those veins skillfully, and extracts the blood an hour after another, until you see the veins that were full of oil; and beware that you do not block the eye with the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cope with only those veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye a green and red collier to corrupt what is more stubborn than the cataract.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot coil all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the eye with soothing things to calm the pain of the eyes, and let it be for some days until the pain is calmed and assured of a hot abscess, then recommence according to this method which is before until it is healthy; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not yet healthy, if it is engendered in the eye that you open on the abscess, there where it must be cleaned, and draws out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, you will see the corruption and blackness, if it has taken on all the appearance of what is its form; and it is called "rough head", and it must be made into a feir inde a .i. chief reont, and it must be pointed like a lime as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the healthy part of the bone that is corrupted, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little so you feel that the corruption is reduced; and do this several times, then restore the healthy part with medicines that are excitants.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the eyes are cloudy, and there is no birth, and the body of the bowel is cloudy, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew and is not apostemized, and bad accidents come, know that it is healthy; if not, if there is another engine than to bring back the fistula to the hole of the nostril according to this form: and it is that you discover the bone a second time by iron, and by bitter medicines, and when it is discovered thus take .I. foret according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and let the fistula be attenuated until the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place on the bone of the forearm, and detach your hand from the eye a little, then turn the entire foret until it pierces the bone and feels the patient through this, since the veins are in it if he holds his hand against his nostril; and then restore the healthy part with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh is born and endures the eyes, thus one sees the matter at the nostril; thus it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Because of the tearing apart of a torn vein.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the torn vein, then open it, and insert a paper thread as if it were a grain of resin, and it is astonishing to see; then if you want to repair it, the procedures are such that you put a needle at the root of the affected part just below, then put another needle where there is a double filament from the affected vein; and make them pierce, and leave the first needle in place according to its disposition; then cover the affected part with a double filament and bind it around the torn vein, and hold it firmly, then remove the needle and put it on the moist eyelid in abundance of water; and let it be until the filaments unite with the vein, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healthy; and never restrain the wound by binding it with a circle of cloth, until it is healthy.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then prick with a subtle spatula which comes in front of the eye, and correct the moist albugeanum and descend below the eyes, and enter there immediately; then hold until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Here is the translation:
des aigues de l’oil	the veins of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have seen the similarity of the veins in the division, and it is necessary to pierce; if you work according to health. It is necessary that you hold the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye firmly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if the eyes are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are on the right; then put the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the thickness of a hair at the white part of the eye at the side of the lesser eyelid, then insert the instrument called "almagda" gently, and turn your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the clear thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the depth of the measure of the spaces which are from the prune-like notch up to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; if you see the opening in this paper by the clarity of the woven fabric, and then put the instrument near where the vein is, then press it down one way after another. If the vein descends now, if the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After resting a little, and if the vein rises again by the second way, put the strength with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not rise, then extract almagda lightly while turning your hand little by little; and then put back into the vein a little of that same gem, and remove from that eye within. Then put besides the eyes stooping or cloudy in oil rosset and abundance of egg, and tie with the healthy eye. Us, and those who are of our time, put on common broiet with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the marrow cannot enter the eye through its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyelashes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which is of this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce the conjunctiva subtly, and do not go too deep in the fontanelle, but make a subtle hole, then inject the marrow as we have said; and at the completion of the work appearing to the patient .i. sleeping, while he sleeps on his back in .j. a dark place; and be deprived of all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark house, and test his vision, and make him see certain things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is necessary that you do not do this during the hour of treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate it, because the water mounts hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If abscesses come, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and address what soothes the abscess; and when it is appeased, then unbind the vision and put on his face .i. a golden rim to cover for some days, and be again in that dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and convert into its cases; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the country of Yrach, who told us that in his country they made an instrument to pierce the marrow, with which they sucked out the water, but I never saw any in our land, nor did I read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of alumga, because those who do not know them go astray; and they should be properly arranged:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And thus the head of the bones of this same subtlety, and the last in four angles alike.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	No time is born or nose flesh joined in various ways, because there are some that seem like scorpions with many feet; and if it has such flesh of fixed color, and if it has soft bone-colored flesh. In this case of those flesh which is soft and not fixed, you should make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and throw the onion at those flesh, and treat them with fire; then grasp what you can sustain in the subtle spatula on one part, so that you know that this flesh is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be coped, open everything .i. of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if you are not mounted above, or an abscess forms, drain it as it should be; and if they are malignant apostemes, hasten to cauterize them until the blood is staunched and all the flesh is burned away, then pour in wine or vinegar and water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the veins do not open, and moisture comes just to the palace, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pass as it should, know that there is new flesh growing in the bone above, although the instruments do not come for cutting: then it is necessary that you prepare .i. a thread of flax slightly thick, and be careful with our hands, and hold between each thumb's width .i. or less; and place the patient's head on the thread at his nose, and draw out in an odorant manner until it comes through the nose inside the mouth; and many times children do so as a game, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other in being like us who are on the thread. Do this until you know that the veins have corrupted that flesh, then draw out the thread, suck out the blood, and wrap the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this .iij. days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of flesh; and then place a cane of plum trees for some days until it is healthy, and if there is need of medicines afterwards, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, where they distill oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or copper, resembling a lamp overturned, like a cane, and guide it thus; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have .i. a handle on the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease occurs on the nose called "telul", and grows and becomes large, so it is visible when looked at; and for this reason you must cover it at the beginning, and remove all hair, then place on it the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay covering until it becomes large, take heed if it is hard, of fixed color, of poor sense: if not touching with iron for it is an encrusted abscess, for when one covers it many times, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of fixed color, and you see that one can cover everything, then look at the patient and cover it with sense and fear, and cure the place with drying and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is covered and bandaged
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when continuous flow comes into one of these cartilaginous joints, it profits little, for in some homes. Therefore, you must take care that this does not happen to anyone, if you see that the wound is fresh and full of its blood; and then join the .ij. veins to a costure, then cure until it is healthy; and if the veins are already disjoined from one part and another, you must scrape all parts of their skin until they heal, then join the .ij. veins to a costure, and restrain, and powder with powdered dragon's blood, and incense burnt; and put on the powders a piece of strong or other plaster, and let it stick by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the suturing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of men who have dens abscesses on their lips, similar to grains of veins, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut into each node, and take them as pinces and cover in each part; then apply the remedy after the incision of vitriol broth, so much that the wound is stained; and then leave it to heal, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the decay of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is an abscess on the gums which the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold them in place with tongs, and cut to its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then put on the spot vitriol powder, or other drying and constricting powders; and if that abscess returns after the incision, and many times happens, if you cut a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of treatment for covering.
des sordens	of the ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are rough and bitter; and sometimes the black, citrus, and greenish teeth, as much as the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become putrid; if it is necessary that you hold the patient's head between your hands, and their jaws be in your care, and take out the teeth or scabs appearing, so that nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other stains, as much as they are worldly; and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good; if not, then recommence to rework on the second day and the third, until you have taken everything; and know that teeth have mastery of diverse forms of treatment for reworking, according to what the work demonstrates, because the root which one removes from the teeth has other forms than those which are between the teeth; and these forms and others will be with you, well-equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay treating as much as you can, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance just up to then one has no excuse for delaying.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Here is the translation:
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth directly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently press it into each part lightly, and remove it as you did previously. And if the tooth is perceived and gnawed, it must be filled with threads, where the roots are; and if it is held subtly in the gums, so that it does not break while extracting; and it must work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care not to break it, and leave a part behind, and return to the patient through the malice of the large root, causing greater pains than before. And beware that you do not act like ignorant surgeons, who in their haste and hardness often break the cartilage, and do not amend what we have mentioned; but they come often by the obstruction of this great illness due to the roots that remain, or because the cartilage breaks, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the socket with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood flows out, which often happens, apply the burnt vitriol powder; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, which one must use to extract teeth first, should be long and pointed, with large handles, so that they do not slip when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let there be large limbs so they do not bend in the traction, and let them be of iron well-made, and let them be toothed to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the traction, it is necessary that you place on the cotton cloth moistened with burrage. One day or two., as long as the limbs are numb, then they put on the clamps called "algefri", from which the head seems like a beak of a sign; and let them be made thus as a lime and it is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to issue into all these clamps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh totally around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", it is to know the palate, from which it is their shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break easily, and if the root jumps through this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, from which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has ten inches, from which there is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools that are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large pincers, from which there is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many of the teeth's instruments are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtly find by themselves their own instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are certain illnesses where the ancients did not teach at all about the diversity of instruments, and it is not broken into a chariot or other bones, or it will rot, if one seeks these instruments that they need, as I have told you, and help with gestures, from which there is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let it be thick and well-held to hold the bone, so it does not slip away, but can hold and support; and then restore the limb with suitable medicines, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if you take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course of the body, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, if it seems that you know the teeth are not born after the tooth, and it is not in its right place, and one cannot make it firm or fasten: then take the root; and if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument which has a shape like a small beak, and let it be of iron sharpened to a point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take the instrument little by little in your hands daily for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can fasten it, then fix it with a thread like this is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the thread of which one makes the needles; and fix the tooth little by little in your hands daily lightly, so that it does not move until it holds; then apply a smooth surface at the end without any roughness, and if the tooth is too pointed and it hurts the tongue, if you need to file the asperity until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth falls out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front tooth falls out, either by percussion or by decay, and the patient cannot chew because it hurts, and you have treated them with medicines that constrict, but it does not work; if you need to restrain it with a thread of gold, for the silver thread turns green and putrid, but the gold does not move at all; and so the thread should be neither too large nor too small, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you want to adjust the teeth, take the thread and double the knot between the sound teeth, then place the teeth among the bad ones, if there are one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then recommence the covering up to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and steadily, so it does not move at all; and so your ligature is at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape. Then cut the threads with a pair of scissors, and assemble them, and replace them between the sound tooth, and set it in place so it does not bite the tongue; and then leave it in place as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the thread breaks, hold it in place with another thread; if it stays in place, it will serve for a long time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the sound teeth, and of the bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, you put it back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and do not get involved with those who are not wise and suffer, and never make the shape of a tooth from an ivory tusk, and you set it in place where the defect is, and hold it in place as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of burning the ligature of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	It never happens that the ligatures which come from under the tongue or naturally, do not grow back; or by accident of a wounded palate; and the operations are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your healthy hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligature of the large one, so much that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is roughness or numbness, and it is suddenly wounded, if you anoint with unguent and cut the large ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift up the water of rose and of hazel, or of cold water, then put under the tongue a linen cloth; and every night, anoint the patient's gums, so they cannot suck. And if a flow of blood comes, put on the head vitriol bruised; and if the wound does not heal, cauterize with a slow cautery, which is good for that; then cure with another cure until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see the flesh of a color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer; and if it is declining into whiteness, and there is moisture, anoint with unguent, and make a subtle spatula, and deliver from one part to another; and if the wound does not heal through your operation, put on vitriol bruised until it is stained, then return to your operation until you treat everything thoroughly; then lift up the water of hazel and of seed, and cure with other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Here is the translation:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You can't press the tongue against this instrument, and you see the abscess, if you take the onion and place it in the amulet, and make the trajectory above where you can; and don't take anything from the tiles with, then cover the instrument, because it is the form that seems a force; and always the head is curved, and one end to the other, and are very agile, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument at hand, so cover it with tourniquets, because it is the form.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one part, and naming on the other part; and when you have covered one of the amulets, so cover the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and warm and clear, and if blood evacuates, so gargle the patient warmly, or apply cures of green pomgranates that are cut up, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is staunched; then cure until it is healthy; and no other time do abscesses grow in the throat besides these .ij. amulets, so cover them thus as the .ij. amulets are applied.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which was a small abscess of little sense; and it had almost closed up the whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the conduit that was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed thus .i. hour or .ij.. And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed .ij. roots through the .ij. perforations of the nose. I hastened to treat her then, and placed an onion in one nostril, then made a trajectory above, and extracted a large portion of pus; then I repeated the procedure on the other side of the nose, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I placed the onion in those abscesses, and covered part of it, and only issued a little blood; and thus was unclogged the conduit of the woman's throat, and she began to drink warm wine, and did not cease to cut into that abscess for a long time; and the abscess recurred again, and refilled the void I had emptied, so much that it grew very large; then I treated her deceitfully and cauterized inside her throat: thus it remained unclogged; and I departed from those regions, and knew only God would do with her after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the vein is deep in the vein, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and when it is thick and round, it is called a "vein". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, and you see that the aposteme is appeased, and it is subtle; then it is necessary to cut. And the one which is round and assembled and not long; and it is sanguine or of fused color or black, then it is necessary to cut into it. For there is great peril for the patient. Then it is necessary, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, by its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; then insert the needle into the vein, and draw it back, and cut with the instruments I have said in the incision of the veins. And it is necessary not to cut more than the superfluousness that is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the veins, and cure until it is healthy. And if the patient has fear of cutting, then it is necessary to use fire cautery instead. And the manner of cautery is sharp and pointed. And it is that the patient puts their head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue against the instrument we have said or the chapter of cautery, and confirms with a lively and sharp movement, so that it is not too dense nor too clear; and in using the movement of this instrument, by which it is formed:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have on the head a veil or om which puts the medicine, as if the movements of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine on the vein; and let the patient sit on their side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth to the medicine inside, so it does not descend into the throat, and the blister; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the vein for a quarter of an hour, until you see it is reduced and the mordications of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into all the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton adheres to the vein; and do this often, until the cauteries are perfected, then let it dry, and apply afterwards for 3 or 5 days. And if you need to renew the fire of the medicine, then rekindle it, and after the cautery, pour out what is inside the vein, from cotton plugged into a pipe, and clarify what is around the medicine; and be raised by sharp cold, and be cured of gagging as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not that of the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a pot, and put aisil, and make boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and in it have an instrument that is arranged in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or copper, and let one of the heads be inserted into the patient's mouth as long as the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, until the eye is mortified; afterwards, repeat often, until the eye dries out, and take care that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do it more frequently than during the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a tuft of egg white into the head, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the tuft of egg white does not allow the vapor to bother the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether, healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens to the throat or spine of a fish, or some other thing; so it is necessary that you extract what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and what does not appear and is retained in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit, so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps by chance the thing will be expelled through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; and attach the sponge to the thread, and then transglutinate; and when it comes to the place, it will be recognized, and then you will extract further; and if it does not come out according to what we have said, take an instrument for probing in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.
