And let the curved instrument be at the head so it can enter more lightly into the throat, and hold the head high upraised; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all may come to harm, nor thrust the bone within; and it is of value that the patient himself thrusts the instrument, because it seems easier thus; if he thrusts below, where he draws it forth evenly throughout the entire instrument, so it may be drawn forth.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the swelling of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No medicine can cure the swelling, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when it does not profit at all, then gaze into the throat of the patient towards the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the swelling, draw it out completely with a small hook, or subtle pincers that are worth it. And if it is not valuable, take a hooked hair, and thrust it into the throat of the patient, then thrust or bend the hooked hair with iron heat, and make it so often. And if you hold the patient's water throughout the day, then take full sight of the cold water, and open the mouth, and gargle without swallowing, and move it with his own hand often; and if you feel the swelling feels the cold, shout.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not shout as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asphaltide, at the instrument that I have told you in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will soon be calmed. And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are charcoal embers, and let it be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and in that perforation let the head of the instrument be; then pour out the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane into his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not issue forth, but comes just to the swelling; and the swelling will now be calmed, and if it does not shout, then recommence the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient to thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and drink no water; and then it is necessary that he urinate freely by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument to which one treats the blood, it is, when one can see it, similar to a curved tenaille entering the throat; and it has the appearance of a beak of a sign, and it has the roughness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the surgeons of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many types of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways, one is in its own appearance, and because of what it holds in moisture. And the second way is through the veins where they are in the body. for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come into joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce, as long as the swelling is mild according to its completion; and if there are such ones that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come from joints, and one leaves them until they are ripe within, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is in the principal member, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; or if it is from the foundation, one should pierce it thus so it is ripe; and it is not necessary to pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for that which is from the foundation, so it does not putrefy within, and becomes inflamed, and creates a fistula; and it cannot be healed in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the signs of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to completion, and it's when the pain is appeased, and the departure from fever, and the diminishing of the pain and of the redness, and the debating and the adjusting of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make sit the perforation or more depending on the location of the abscess, and where it appears most; and let the perforation be of long duration of the body, and if the abscesses are in hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no putridity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these cases, it bursts according to the member. And when the abscess is in a fleshy area, it is worthwhile to let the perforation be until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce beforehand, the body will be filled with much putridity; and perhaps the lips and the inner parts of the body will harden. And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the size of the body, according to the member that has need of it.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez. des soros	of ulcers
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where the wounds of a chief vein come from small abscesses, and are ways for us to be in tiles, just like the joint of a gully, and there are many similarities. There is fat and such things where there is moisture, just like poultices; and if there are hard and pierous things to cut with, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act against it. And the work of the cutting is that you try everything .i. instrument which is called "entromissoire", from which the form comes afterwards, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then it swells from above the length. And when the moisture is evacuated, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately when you leave nothing; then apply cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; otherwise, in water and in oil, and apply to the wound, and let it be until another day; and this corrects what has remained of the nit. And then reapply the cotton, just as before, on the second day, and the third, as long as you know well that it does not remain of the nit; then treat the ointment wound according to what is suitable, so that it may be healthy. And if the abscess holds .i. much fat, then cut according to this form, from the length; and apply your remedies, and scrape off all around, and put all your treatment in order to cure the wound where it lies; and if the artery acts against you, then do what I have told you afterwards. And do the same for the abscess if it is pierous, and of cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting into the pierous abscess and the moisture is lighter, for they are of little blood. And if there are some of these abscesses or chief where there is no moisture, and of these .i. abscesses that I cut open or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess just like a rotten stone, rough and whitish, and could not break it; and if one had not made any effort, one would have done as well to make a wound from a stone. In other abscesses coming from the chief, for those that come from the chief of children and the roots of the ears, the operation should be done in at most three days, depending on how much it is necessary to remove the swelling; and the treatment should be done as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of the tumors
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times have abscesses occurred at the neck, and beneath the arms, and in the groins, and many times they appear elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and are entwined with each other. And each tumor is specifically located on its side, just like the swelling and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities between these tumors are many. There are those that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health. In this case, you see a good disposition in the body, and it appears similar to the color of the body, and changes on each part and is not airy as the veins at the neck or in the artery, and is not deep; so it is necessary to cut above them, and to dissect each part, and to expose the two levres of the heart as oncines, if you are skilled, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and take it slowly, and be careful that you do not touch the nerve or the vein, and do not let the spatula slip, lest you cut too much, so you do not touch what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut into the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to operate, then put vitriol broiet in the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; and let it be until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to heal. And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you accomplish it; then inquire into your duty if there remain small tumors, if you cut and mend them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the tumor, it does not matter that you cut that tumor at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with much cotton plugged into an Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire tumor, it is necessary that you reassemble the two levres of the wound, and sew them now, so that there remains no excess flesh due to the size of the tumor. It is necessary that you intend to cut at its root, and remove the excess, and sew as we have said. Those tumors that hold excess flesh, pierce it where it appears dead; and pierce it thus as described above, depending on the case, then treat it with ointment and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well mended, cure it with ointment and heating charm, until it is healthy.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke and talked of the incision of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and it is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cleaned; and one should not help with this, because all the veins and the pormon of the patient are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the gullet, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it between two or three circles, or a small cutting through, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cutting through the syphac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and thus it is necessary to make the cut at the section of the epiglottis where there is no cartilage, and the vessels are far from inquiry.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the masters are afraid, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to all the surrounding area, then cut the heart as far as it reaches the trachea; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see nothing, and then cut through the syphac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the flow of the trachea which stops being fruitful through the place that is broken, and by the defect of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and let the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound with a gentle touch, and sew everything beneath the sense without the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, so it may be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	One should not do this just so long as the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and lacking in breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then one should cut on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is protected from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and therefore command the old one to let the open wound be so that the evil of the disease passes, and it has passed in three days or in two days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they command to bandage the wound and treat, until it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took a small knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the sinews of the arm.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called for by the healer, and I found it thus as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and saw well that it had not been properly covered with a dressing or bandage except for the throat, and the veins were issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healthy.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and I had not harmed the maiden for she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Because I see that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a jaundiced person, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural and accidental; or natural does not have any obstruction.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is according to two ways, one of which is similar to a thick swelling in us, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not seem to work with fierce fires except in the one that is small, and he tries and searches everywhere for the entire internal arrangement.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it thus as if in a thick swelling, and it does not penetrate to any vein, then it stops, just as we stop the nose, and he draws to his entire coffin, if there is a point.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well everywhere, and heal it so that it covers, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of treating us, which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and therefore it is suitable that I should point out all the differences that exist between them and this.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that this is a crisis and fever, as long as the inflammation has passed, and it is accompanied by putridity; then the fever and crisis settle.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the ninth node it has no heat nor fever nor pain, and contains a flux, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins thus like a jaundice, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, whether grave, or moist, and many colors are thus as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the ninth node, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "intermediate", according to what its form will be or the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about the abscesses of the nodes is that you take or touch the moist place where you find it in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, so that you know that the instruments have perceived the core, then according to the greatness of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the entromissoire, and take care in this that it knows how to make a good scar.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moist corrupts the short, whatever its color may be, thus they do as I have said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and after the entromissoire no moistness comes, it knows that it is fatty, thus they do then in a cross, and take it with pincers, and lightly scrape each part and turn the cotte where it lies, so you pull it straight with the nail;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it straight, then pull it by pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if he remains still, then returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if he stays still a little, and the wound does not grieve him, then apply to the wound some corrosive powders, and hold the wound steady, and put on soothing things to calm the hot abscess, and treat with other treatments until he is healthy;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is a large wound, then cut the lips of the wound, and treat what injures the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is bursting, it's contrary or otherwise, hasten and apply the liquid of vitriol, and let it stay for two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and then repose the ebullition of blood; then return to cauterizing what has been delayed from the outset.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here is the translation:
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles with which one cuts the sorescles, and are of citrin iron, or of silver, or of copper, and those that are yellow are more experienced in piercing the knots of fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the lancets are very similar, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are lancets that have three knots in three kinds similarly;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if there are lancets that have three knots, and they are of three kinds; and if there are lancets that have two knots, and lancets with a single knot only, and they are of three kinds; and all this is necessary in their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is to those who make them cutting, and of such there are some that do not cut more than a part, from which one scrapes the nails, because one does not touch the vein nor the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introjections are the alkaline remedies applied to the handles, so that the patient does not perceive themselves at the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three kinds: large, small, and moderate, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use more than the clear charcoal, as for legs, and arms, and limbs, and similar things.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and many times one makes another small instrument, similar to thongs of fisticuffs, according to this form, where one staunches blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one places it many times at the healthy spot which joins the veins, and the arteries, and many times one encounters according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Many times they swell the limbs of certain men when their corruption begins, so much that they seem like feminine limbs;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they become lazy and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, if one knows how to operate according to this form of these lines, right up to G.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and apply the medicine in a gentle circular motion, then assemble the lips of the wound to suture, and care for it until it is healthy;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and the breast is sloping downwards, and it is amazed by its greatness just like it happens with women, if they make a .ij. ribcage above, through similar fissures;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	because one is holding onto the other at the end of one and of the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line B to the line G;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin which is between the .ij. lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it does not heal, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the deterioration of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it be until it digests the residue and fat, then heal it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	from abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that grow under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofulous tumors which have ribs, and there is only moisture that they contain.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Here is the translation:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire swelling that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with much cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply a dressing to make it healthy again.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, do as we have said in cases of scrofula, and if the wound becomes swollen, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin is sewn which is above, then often come abscesses, and also it has swollen veins and abscesses.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one recognizes it thus when it is by the artery, then are the abscesses long in depth;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel strangulation; and when it is by the vein, then are the signs of fever appearing;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to touch this abscess, and similarly when it is under the arms and in the angles and in the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary then to avoid the iron treatment, and the one who is at the head must avoid it also, and in the one who has an inflamed artery, a bandage is placed above the skin of the loin;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then open the incision at the shoulder blade, and carefully separate the artery from the tiles, until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then put a needle underneath it, and make it pierce just to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then puncture the spot which is between the two ligaments of an intermuscular space, as far as the blood flows out of it, and thus release the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the treatment that brings down the swelling, until the ligament is freed;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal this one of anointing coming to this one, so long as it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscesses are because of the size of the vein, it is necessary that you hold with your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin;
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then put the needle beneath the skin that you hold with your hand, and make it pierce, and it has a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then lance the abscess, as I have told you, or bind it with one of these parts as one binds a twisted thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread does not come out, if it breaks another needle altogether at the spot of the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut into the abscess as much as the excess flows out, then cut away the excess from around the heart and let go what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a clean cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply remedies of tents and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nostrils
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Here is the translation:
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And it happens more often with the joints and the two toes or where there are joints, and this is a severe abscess, and its color appears like the color of a dead body, and it is in many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one strains forcefully, the patient feels pain, and it is not as deep in the body, but beneath the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it moves badly in all directions, and does not go either forward or backward, neither below nor above, and the one who is in joints cannot be treated with iron: perhaps there will be a contraction by chance;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is at the head or at the forehead, makes the skin on the Spartumile (a type of skin lesion).
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, if you hold it with a bandage, and cut at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if you support it with a poultice, and scrub, then scrape the bone and bring the wound together at the seam, and cure until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of thick, hanging lumps

dou chancre	swollen tumor

de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Here is the translation:

Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal then the place of sudden wounds with powder, which we have said or treated with powders, and if you cover beyond measure, and it goes to the surface, it will not harm at all; heal then, as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	due to retention of urine

des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blood or pus accumulates in the bladder, where putrefaction is assembled, and you see them distill aqua and medicines, if you make all the instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:

de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the methods of stone, and the extraction with assembled medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone in the kidneys as they rain, and all the signs, and how one must operate on the size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the kidneys in the bladder often happens to children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder with subtlety; and I openly declare, and greatly afflict the patient's penis, and they often repeat, and then become inflamed; and many of these jumps are the foundations; and it's easy to cure children until they are three years old, and it's very grievous in the elderly, and it's as if midway, for those who are between youth and old age; and it's easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere. de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Since the stone is often found in women, and if it happens to anyone, then the cure is difficult, and is defended by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to uncover the mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Here is the translation:
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this arm is from weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the joints, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is declining yellowish, or without red, or black, or watery pale, and this happens more.

Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in its own fabric, then the abscesses are ripe with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg.

puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then he should sit on his left, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the ribs near the hollow of the groin.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula-like instrument, and cut the skin of the joints within the length just to the point where it pinches, and let your incision be entirely straight while dividing the skin of the joints up to the white spot, and carefully scrape off the thin skin according to what you can do.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the white spot plainly with a large perforator, and extract all the water, and then put in your hooks, and the white spot will be above; and do not touch the joint of the hip, but let the white spot come out solely; cut everything or in pieces from the same side subtly, so that if you do not cut well, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the vein bursts for a lot of work, if you reassemble it in its place when you will have completed the vein of the white spot; then assemble the two lips of the joint of the hip into one suture, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the vein corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you raise the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cut the joint at all the suspended places, and extract the vein, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the wound is assembled in two parties gathered, know that they are two branches; if you cut the other party just as you did the first alignment, then suck out the blood, and put into the wounded place a moist ointment of oil rose.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put afterwards another moist dressing in wine and oil, and put on the two cushions, and put above doubled drapery, and tie it all together with the lien that is according to this form.
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two drapery, and fill with lint according to this resemblance, and let them be assembled by stitching in the girdle of the arm, and one of the heads takes hold at the bottom just up to the back, and another at the part of the finger; and another two heads on the two angles, and so is all assembled the restraint in the loop of the arm.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and no time is medicine applied to this cautery of fire in the form of iron, and it is that you take a subtle cautery scalpel, and cut the skin of the cushions, and be heated as we have said, so that the white sap that contains the wound is uncovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the fire cautery according to this method, and pierce that place with an onion-shaped instrument, and scrape with this subtle cautery burn:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And take the cup in all the ways that you can, so that you scrape everything; and beware that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salutary; and beware of the corruption of blood, and beware of the bad practices of surgery.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing makes you do the opposite, or an abscess bursts or corruption of blood or other thing, if you heal what makes you do the opposite, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is faint-hearted, and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horribleness, then make a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain through the signs that we have said that the aqueous humor is there.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Here is the translation:
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let it absorb the remaining water, then treat it until the wound is healthy.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and let the white cloth not allow the water to issue from the mouth of the wound, if it is necessary that you insert a tube or instrument through which one treats the watery discharge of hydropics; thus the shape is formed before; and enlarges .i. a little the wound, and knows that the water returns, and is assembled after 22 months or thereabouts, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the treatment of this disease, there is fear in many dispositions, because it seems to me that many are worth leaving;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from corruption, and likewise from bad humors; and it is in most cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive bitter anger and anguish, which is spread through bad humors, or from a blow.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no finding of pain, and it is a grievous abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there are painful abscesses and piercing, and of a dark color, and sometimes it comes from a narrowing of the artery, or an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to a narrowing of the artery, it is recognized by the formation of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it with your hand.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	That which is made from an inflammation of the vein is recognized by its appearance at the point of tender touch of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well make a cut on this similarity, and on other scars;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the skin of the joints, then stretch the vein above, and remove the white crust from the surface, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the vein is already inflamed with these new scars, then it is necessary that you remove the vein, and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is attached to the crust, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension, and cut around it again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of flesh is behind the true skin, then it is necessary that you take all of it, and extract the humor, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the operations are accomplished, then fill the wound with mulled wine and rose oil, then heal it with other treatments until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	These are abscesses enveloped in an envelope-like swelling resembling a .i. boil, with the softening of the groin,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient must complain greatly when they go;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this illness is well nearly as painful as this one beforehand,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a high seat, then bind the suspender of the loins below your two fingers,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	For all the vessels that are close to the edge, and prick the masters, and stretch them out strongly;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut into the spatula-like instrument, cutting deeply through to the spot where the vessels are, until they are discovered;
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape off each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then fix a needle where it has a double thread, and tie it to the first vein where the blood flow has come, and then tie it again to another vein;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then they take a straight measurement, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupting moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heal the wound as if the others or inject a poultice, so that no vessel bursts that nourishes one of the intestines;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by this means no harm comes, and if all the vessels come together, then it is necessary to treat the intestines with all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of this face
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrences of this ulcer are by the section that comes from the face, or the extension onto the belly in the part of the loins, because the intestines descend from that treatment to one of the flanks;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this treatment is from the face or from its extension, and these two manners of many causes come from it: either from percussion, or from a fall, or from a blow, or from lifting a heavy weight, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the face, are that it comes gradually and slowly, in long tension, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and it is the abscesses equal right up to the peritoneum, because the swelling presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the swelling, which makes sudden pain come at the beginning, and it is diverse abscesses appearing beneath the skin, and this is because of the issue of the intestine and the body's weakness from the swelling.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it descends beneath the ribs with the intestine, and is retained inwardly, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron to fear, because they think it will hurt them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the surgery is that you instruct the patient to reintegrate the intestine with their hand inside the wound, if they can re-enter.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then be supported on his neck between your hands, and lift the hips.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch out the cord above, and cover all the skin of the joints from the loin.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then thrust inside the veins of the waist, uncinate according to what you have mastered for opening the wound, and be such that the eyes can issue forth.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the skin that is beneath the leather of the joints, so much that the white skin beneath should be uncovered on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then put your finger index in the one that follows the joint, in the one that is between the white skin beneath the leather of the vein, and between the second skin,
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and separate that which is behind the vein, and between the second skin; and then move the vein to the right hand within the curve of the joints, and hold the white skin above with your left hand, and lift the vein to all the skin towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to stretch the vein upwards, and dislocate that which is behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and if you have two fingers in it, if there is a point of the intestine wrapped around or white and hard, and if you do not find anything, then it bursts into the belly below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle or it has a large thread made of ten threads, and push it into the rear part of the soft syfac, which is behind the skin of the intestines; after the waist, then cut the heads that appear as threads, so long as there are three threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and tie the syfac, which we have said is behind the skin of the intestines, with a strong thread of two threads.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the heads of the threads, and tie them firmly with two threads, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter into it, lest an abscess forms there.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and set the bandage according to the first long band, two inches of that one, and after these two bands leave enough space which is beneath the heart of the joints, the width of a finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg produces; then cut in the part which is beneath the skin of the joints, until the saneness corrects it, and the swelling, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then mix the millet in oil, and put it on the wounds, and I will mix the bandage that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And no time is it cauterized with a white cloth as we have said, after the incision, because of fear of deterioration of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens often, and let the vein gush as much as it pleases; and if it delays in healing, so be aroused by warm water, and put on what we have said, until it heals.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then heal the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who knew how to make the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is done thus as the ram's horn which is assembled on the nose, in such a way that you bind the veins, after cutting lightly underneath.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cauterize in the middle, and treat the abscess of those who have a rupture, until the veins are clear; and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	No rupture ever occurs in the groin, as we have said, and opens the loins; and do not descend into the intestines as to the bowels, and if they do descend, it is little, and repair all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and always, if it stays too long at this point, the wound or abscess grows, so that the intestines descend.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this has happened through the extension of the soft tissue which is like a cloud, as we have said, because it is stretched out, then becomes softened and weakens the limbs and opens them.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and no cure is made with iron in this manner.
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient places himself on his back between your hands, then feels the limb of the injured part according to the quantity of two fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the soft tissue that is under the skin which is swollen, then take the remedy and place it on the apparent limb of the soft tissue.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and you press on the fontanelle of the belly, then cut the jugulars appearing on the syphac on the head of the vein, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the vein, and do not touch the syphac point where the vein extends to another thing, just as I have made you aware in the treatment of the curvature of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then heal by healing the wounds. And when you touch the threads, if it is undefined and heal the wound, so that it may be healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphac is constrained, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cauteries are moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the thighs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the thighs is softened in some men, because the flesh that is within is mollified, and it is easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure, to make the patient sit on his back, and to cover the skin that is mollified with natural skin; then assemble the .ij. lips to a suture, and if you see, first remove the superfluousness of the mollified skin at .iij. sutures or .iiij. firmly; then cover between the sutures, and cure it as the other wounds, until it is healthy, and sews the thread.
dou chastrement	of the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	I know that punishments are established in our law, and therefore I prefer not to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to do so except for .ij. manners: one of which is that the masters respond when asked, and heal; and the other, because we often have need of punishing some beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts. I say therefore that punishments are made according to .ij. manners: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one that we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water, so long as the skin is mollified and pendant; then take it with your hand, so long as it is reset and you no longer feel it. Of the punishment of size: it is necessary to hold the beast, and press the skin of the thighs with your left hand, then suspend it, and cover each part with a .i. cope, when you have well searched them; and leave none of the subtle tissue and the subtle tissue that is under the vessels; and this manner of punishment is more moderate than that which is done by attraction, because at attraction sometimes some thing of the thighs remains, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	Here is the translation:
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.
