de la tentigene	of the tetanus
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tetanus is a twisted cord on the natural part, so much it is too ugly to see; and some women have had it as large as a hand, and that's the treatment. It is necessary that you remove the excess of tetanus from your hand or fingers, and gently stroke; and don't go too deep in the wound, lest corrupted blood flows, then treat with another remedy until it is healthy; and on another twisted cord that grows at the mouth of the marrow, and the remedy, and by chance it bursts forth, and it resembles a cow's disease, and for this reason they called it "cow disease" in old times. It is necessary that you treat it, as we have said regarding tetanus, and the treatment until it is healthy.
de erratique	of the erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the pertus is small; and it is born naturally, or occurs by accident due to illness that comes about; or it is a twisted cord, or subtle and hidden, and it is made in the marrow, or in the costal area, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, and childbearing, and by chance the flowers have; and the knowledge of this is through the gaze of the baile. The stoppings are near appearing, if you want to know. If it is a subtle and hidden cord, and it is near the .ij. livres, hasten, and turn thus: put your .ij. fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then bend the .ij. livres forward, so that the subtle and hidden cord is turned, and is over the stoppings; then take a linen cloth, and anoint it with oil, and place it on the spot, and guide the woman to home every day, so that she cannot conceive. And if the cord is hard and hidden, it is necessary that you treat it with the spatula-like instrument resembling a foil of myrtle. If the stoppings are of a new cord, suspend it at the navel and stroke; and take the medicines cleansing the blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, ensemble abun d'uef; then apply a large poultice; so that the wound cannot conceive; and thus it will be long, and apply a tent of linen thread; then treat with other treatments until it is healthy. And when there is a new cord in the marrow, it is necessary to treat it according to this method, if it is not an aposteme that grows. For at the growing aposteme which is in the marrow, one must not touch or do anything.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. de l’enfantement	of the swelling

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to put the limb back in its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, to which one adds the books; and at 10 turning points as 10 heads of the ligaments.

Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	Here is the translation:

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation perceived, thus it has been stifled by subtle signs.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	it is necessary therefore to apply a poultice that it perceives the subtle sign with its finger, and does not perceive it at all through a spatula or ague, and adjusts the bandage so it does not touch it.

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the bottom foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from beneath the foundation are nodulation, and larger than those that come from beneath the foundation of the body, or in the space of the adjacent parts,

des emorroydes	of the sinewy parts
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Sinewy parts are according to two manners: either they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they cut off the blood immediately.

et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and hold them at your fingers, then cover, and sprinkle above some warm powders that are in the fire of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	where you cauterize as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then heal with other healings until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot issue forth, then clisterize the patient with a harsh and bitter cluster to clean that which is in the foundation, so that they can issue forth openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient cannot take it, and their vein is far from the foundation, then it is a light cure;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them by your finger or the nails, and catch, then cure as we have said, so that they be healthy, and fear the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you make the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it on a needle, and then draw the thread above and make pierce the needle from another part, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too large; and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one for correcting the superfluity of blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a piece of cloth soaked in oil rose or cerate, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he should rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it cool down as much as it congeals, and when they are cooled, if you apply treatment of anointing and other treatments, until it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	you dry out the mucus or fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of mucus in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you make a poultice at the point of a spatula or on an ulcerated spot, which does not allow it to become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal as soon as it is swollen so that it becomes healthy.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then restart the treatment more strongly than before, so that it heals much, and becomes scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal as soon as it is healthy.
dou fremit	because of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Here is the translation:
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the chill is found, and one feels it as if dead from cold, and it comes throughout the whole body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a string from a bird's feather, or a strong feather of a vulture, and place that string on the cold spot, so that the circles surround the cold spot entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all around the string so that you grasp it entirely around the cold spot, and put it in the front, and extract the cold spot from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make it in the form of a cane of iron or copper, and be subtle underneath and stretch above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not perceive, for you must hold with your finger and press; and if you see, if you cauterize the trembling flesh, as it is before or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of theclyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make aclyster of silver or copper, or of tin alloy or maillet; and never make one of these small and large instruments, according to those who are accustomed to them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that one uses in the treatment of children and which are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large cluster is above large, where the belly is tied according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the chest is perceived from within; and it has a perforation on one side .ij., and in the other .i.;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly be where one puts the medicines of a bladder of beast or of parchment, and let it be perceived all around with many small perforations,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and let there be between each perforation .i. a space of an inch, then put in these perforations .i. strong thread of twisted thread, crooked in .x. or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a sack;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, if you hold the instrument in front of a strong thread, then cleanse; and that's the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clister with oil or egg white, or similar thing, then insert it lightly:
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then sprinkle the ministers with their two hands together, so that it be all visible, then extract the clister, and raise the patient's legs to the bench,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to issue, let it flow as much as it can; and if he sleeps one night entirely, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat him for a disease of bowel obstruction, and the medicine hastens to expel it, then recommend it until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or an abscess, then let the enema be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously stated in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by blow of stone, and cut of sword and of dagger, or of lance or of stick or of arrow, or of similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the feet, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the remedy will come into its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if it takes care of itself, it's a matter of setting stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you carefully treat the abscessed swelling: if you make it almost healthy in the head measurement, so that little blood comes from the wound, and the healing is on the opposite side of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and abstain the patient from repletion of wine and coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to get healthier, so let his meat be reduced, and do not drink wine, nor eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, abscesses heated by coming blood, cotton soaked in rose oil soothingly, or in wine steeped.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, put it on the wound, as long as it is fresh and its blood is not moved by air or powder, which I will tell you a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the patient's condition has changed, put it on some ointments, as long as they are healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a slash of a spear and similar things, and the lips cannot be assembled by themselves, then assemble them by stitching, as I will tell you about wounds of the belly, of the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered to the bone, and it is deep, and does not hold but for a little, then cover it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore firm flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat large pieces of meat, if they taste and smell roasted, like pork, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or acquire putrid matter, and it does not adhere to the bone, then remove all the putridness, and throw it far away, then apply the treatment.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has entered into the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, seek out the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not benefit, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and it is that you apply this powder which dries in this way so that the wound heals.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of the powder is: take incense, one part; dragon's blood, two parts; living chalk, three parts, and powder subtly.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the plaster, and hold it firmly in place, until it adheres well and joins with all its sap.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, so that it does not become inflamed; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And often one makes a poultice of hot ashes, when one has not the incense nor the blood of dragon, but that the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arsenic has moved the wound, meanwhile in this state, one does not put less of this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it pours forth a flow.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the other wounds as long as they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then hold it steady with subtle pinches;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the breaks of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, if there is no other remedy than to let the treatment, and not to put anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not to put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be soothing, thus heat the water in sweet oil, and mix it with rose oil, and cool the water thus in sweet oil.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other wounds of the mine according to this manner, and anoint them with moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut and bind with bandages, then treat until it be healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, then prick or pierce lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize, that is the way to master it.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and the conduct is guarded, because that's where the food goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	Here is the translation:
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it firmly, and let it be for some days, then cure the joints with ointments until it is healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, remove them gently so you can, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound putrefies;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be disinfected and aligned with the outlet;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then perform the treatment as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from a wound of a spear or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow from a spear or a knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound is ventilated, for if the patient does not expel air: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put the powder at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage that does not penetrate deeply into the wound.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the body, and open the sore.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I will put an attractive bandage on it, and bind it three times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have a bandage, put much cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and have the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 2 days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there does not come a spasm, nor an evil tremor of the heart, which is not a sign of alteration.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good dispositions, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds with tents and other treatments, until they are healthy.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if she cannot heal, and operate, then know that there is a fistula; if the treatment is as one must do it.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether in front or on the back, then treat what is before.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, of stitching; and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has caught pieces, then cauterize the wound, and remove the false feathers if they are dislocated.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not dislocated, then let the wound putrefy, then alleviate the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds to other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	about the obstruction of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The obstructions of the belly are great and moderate and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound often times the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, which prevents the intrusion of pus;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the injury is worse, and no time is better than a small wound than a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one cannot put back into place the internal organs, unless they are replaced gradually and carefully.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell so much that they feel cold, if they return to their place,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to heal the lesser wound, because one can reset the intestine in its place rather than others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the four common stitches have to do with the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitching of other wounds of the body and four other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and however they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will describe each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and none of the intestinal contents are forced out.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and grievous thing is to put back, this is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	where for the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	where for the fact that the intestine is swollen by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is frostbitten, heat it up partially in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soften a sponge or a cloth with warm water and gently lay it on top,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	where you apply heat by squatting and piercing and puncturing,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine until the inflammation is eliminated;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and many times they make these restraining bands, and it is better to remove them by untying.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling go away, if you moisten the intestine with water or a warm potion and evil humors are cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by that it is alleviated, the entrance to a little of things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little wound at the instrument where one gathers the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to moderate the heat
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut without great necessity that it has;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments for making an incision:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut deeply into the curve and do not deviate, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines burst forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you reset it to its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	see you in a power, for this is worth muscles.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is on the lower part beneath the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part beneath the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if you put the head and the foot higher than the parts below,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is on one of the injured parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you find that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to manage what I say in large and minor wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	In small wounds, use what you have prepared.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then you hold between your hands, I minister pitifully who draws out all the treatment with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and gather the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and it is the common manner of stitches,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Then let the top of the wound heal, I do not hasten it, and I fix a needle or there is a strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the skin with the skin of the hip, with the skin of the sphac,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin within, so that you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the head of the hip to the assembly of the sphac;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then hold back with a double thread inside the needle of the finger,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the heads of the wound quickly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then let it be in a space, and fix another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the double thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing so according to what you have learned about the needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the whole wound is closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be moderate, between subtle and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the subtle needles take in all the flesh, and those that are too large cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because it is necessary for them to be moistened;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and soft skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so they do not accumulate and open the wound before the scab;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then remove the heads of the needles, so they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and you hold taut threads on the head of the needles to keep them steady
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it suffices to insert a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second cauterization is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you gather the two heads of skin and the two heads of flesh together at a single point, where there is a strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these heads all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then reset the needle at the part where you started, in the manner that one cuts the threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each vertebra, the size of a lesser finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this vertebra belongs to the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I found a wound that one of our men had in the belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was injured by a dagger,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and it was a wound more than a palm long
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was well of the intestines, nearly two palms of length
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and it was a wound in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned the intestine then, when it had been without food for 23 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and was the wound sewn up to 15 days, and it healed, and was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had given up that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not heal with ointment, for I stood in a place where one found none, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put on it a cotton dressing often twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healthy.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Here is the translation:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and prick the part that is defective just up to the point within.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart in a straight line, if you have placed the head of the siphaeus or costal or where you have pricked with the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce another part of the defective area within just up to the point.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew thus as the pelleteer makes the pelts,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and you let one side of the bandage be loose, and take it up on the other, until the entire dressing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of dressing, which Galen described properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	it is so like a fountain, which naturally assembles the broken parts together,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one head of the bandage to the other head, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or a pointed instrument close by, and make it pierce the skin slightly.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the juices of the blood flow out;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it pierce the part that is defective just up to the inner cavity,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the juices of the blood flow out;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make a perforation on one side and the other of the weakened part just up to the inner edge, in another head of the Miraculum which are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen says this in his book, and no one bears witness to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should stitch the belly with many needles, or there is a thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should thrust an needle from one part, and another from elsewhere, in the manner of those who sew up wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is a wound more grievous than others in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound in all its blood, thus that the artery has moved.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you put back in order the intestine, and sew up the cut; then apply the powder soothing charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the artery has moved, so put no ointment that is present, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew up the sutures, and the membrane;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with the others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to gather pus, a lot of cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it many times a day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not have mastery of other medicines in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not affect the main limbs,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if it is necessary that you apply a light bandage in oil of temperament warm, or in oil rose,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it between the fingers, and beneath the soles;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or prickling in the belly, and many times it happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they apply a cluster of black wine, and meanwhile the porridge reaches up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it penetrates deeply, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is because of the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach to its natural passages.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the suture jumps from the wound, reset it back as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turned towards white or black, it is necessary that you lift the black spot, which is a sign of bad blood that comes from it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the indices of the heads pendant during the part below the wound until it is far enough to alleviate the extraction when the nerves are quiet, and the wound is relaxed.
de la routure dou boueil	from the twisting of the gut
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is swollen, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one can restore it in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced in the belly by a spear.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and it was a wound on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and there ensued the evacuation and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to subtily treat until it was healthy, and the wounds soothed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sweat, I doubted that the patient had a pain in his stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no point of pain, but remained in better disposition, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied up in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take firm stitches with large threads, then assemble the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the patient has opened their mouth, if they place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if they strain their mouth thus;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then they grasp the head, and it holds thus so that it cannot dislocate,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then place another finger afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and cut open the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head settles into the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the intestine with a subtle thread that is taken from the intestine of a beast,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	Take the head of this gut thread that is very much disentangled,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then attach it to the head of this thread, namely a subtle twisted flaxen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reset it in its natural position;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of suturing wounds is not otherwise than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and large, similarly when it is in one of the intestinal gut, if there is no ingenious remedy, because of subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and similarly when it is swollen and burst open.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the true nodulation of hard and white, where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also hairy like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it appears clear and thin, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times sufficient;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healthy, and there is no flesh.
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is not except by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, through the small passage of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or through its evil nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	where for this he has hard crust within, and on the lips, which does not let him have crust;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where he has too much of a bump;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the flesh is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	for it is that the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	for in the property where the region is slow in digestion, and slow in health, and inflamed by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula, which is done by surgical operation.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the spleen, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in any of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	to the spine of the back, or to some joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it reaches the property of the principal member, and similar limbs.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if it has any fistula that does not move near the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you examine the view, if you take a rod of iron or steel, so the fistula is straight, if it is ready.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, if it seeks a subtle probe of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the probes fold back within the twisting;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot search well by probing,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if one catheterizes through one of the passages,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one passage to another, and it is clarified;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you seek to know by your power if there is a bone or nerve, and it is shaved in the background,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and the place where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you will truly know the limb or where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in one of the limbs that I have told you, if the cope follows what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and bone for the fracture and the rotten flesh that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment as long as it is healthy,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well formed in the right place, it is necessary that you cut in a perpendicular direction, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put moist applications in medicine agua, and the joints just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the excess flesh which is accumulated at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments in the wounds, clear and healthy flesh, so that it be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if he is not healthy through this, then he should be cauterized as we have said
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if his bone is corrupted by the fistula, then he should be treated.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve is not grieved or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then you should remove it so that the corruption is completely removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the treatment of things straying so much that they are healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and renders void as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not led just to the fountain:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it discovers and seeks as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and stop all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, it's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deeply rooted, so you cannot come to an end;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with tongs.
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction instrument is suitable for that,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, so remove them completely, do not leave a single one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you burn with fire and moisture, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place on the wound something that promotes suppuration.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the pus is formed between the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have less difficulty with the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a large bone, such as of leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove only the corrupted part so that the blackness is completely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of corrupted flesh, and it reaches close to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to burn and cut all the way to the corruption, and then to treat until it be healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that befell a certain man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take an example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about thirty years, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the materials came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and had no way to evacuate for opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctor, in their foolishness, operated so much that they opened up to the abscesses,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in corrupting many materials, and it became a fistula, and they came to have many holes that all the filth and moisture of the body flowed;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many doctors made a cure within two years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was afflicted, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which corrodes through the perforations to a large body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body became red from youthful strength, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I touched a tent in one of these perforations, and then felt all the perforations.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one vein comes against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut into one of the openings as far as I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption went up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I seized upon that which appeared to me as the corrupted bone, and I thought there was no other corruption, except for that which I had seen;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and thus begins to restore the wound with medicines soaked in long tension, and cannot be sewn;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then he begins again, and uncovers the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and the decay, and then stopped it, and thought of sewing up the wound;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do so much that I cut into one palm of the bone, and thrust it forth with all its marrow;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then the restoration of medicines; and he was quickly healed and relieved suddenly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and did not need to start the work again for the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often blood was evacuated, but he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and it grew on the bone of the shoulder a hard callus, and was of good disposition and had no harm nor opposition in every way, neither to alleviate nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take the bandage, and stretch it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command that it be stretched high above;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another bandage on top of the first one, larger than the first bond, and bind it to the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and hold the head steady, so that you draw out the corrupted flesh from beneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the bone where you see swelling, so that the swelling does not bruise the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a probe or a tubular instrument beneath the bone to remove the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to cauterize as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to cauterize again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not appear so, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if the whole skin is discolored; then put a hot iron underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then one should cauterize from one part to the other the corruption, and let the cautery be done according to the length of the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut into the corrupted joint, and sew the bone or it contains on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of the joints, then there is no other anguish except to cut through;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand, or in the finger of the foot, then it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but however it is necessary that you inquire into that corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and you should anoint it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not cause opposition;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the sockets for covering these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the joints,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each similarity of work with its instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that you will show the instrument with which you have mastered, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and testify about the ways of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you propose the instrument with which you have mastered, according to what it suits him.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head perishes either due to density or due to excess.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have applied the medicine to that corrosion through the treatment of remedies, and they do not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by means of death, or through evil, which is a greater fault, of the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness spreads, then it goes to those corroding of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; if you hasten to cope with it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and this is through the impact of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar things,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Here is the translation:
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just to the hand, if the cope reaches the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach just to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, if the cope reaches the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it does not deserve any remedies except the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and all thus done when the corrosion comes or goes: if it comes to the first joint, then the cope reaches beyond another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then amputate the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it reaches the leg, then amputate at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to amputate or sever the limb is that you tie it above and below;
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister's hand downwards, and another minister's hand upwards,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you dissect the flesh that is between the two ligaments at a spacious latitude, so that the bone becomes uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cover or sew, and put a layer of linen on each part, so that the sewing does not touch the healthy skin,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient another wound and abscess to heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if the blood flow decreases when you operate, then cauterize the limb hastily.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	where you apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then wrap the numb limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to a certain man in our city:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed to come from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion came first in his finger toe, so much that it consumed the entire toe;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to amputate the toe, and was cured;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corruption returned in his hand finger, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put them on things rebounding after the purification of the body, and cannot stop the ulcers;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it seems that I passed the hand, and I did not want, that I had hope of rebounding the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubted also that if I cut off his hand, it would not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was feeble; and he despaired all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and hold fast his hand, and he will be healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not found it stated elsewhere that because of this, one does something else, if one has mastery.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does an abscess come to a clear skin, and it stays for so long that it makes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they break and burst, and the pus jumps out, and the veins become empty, just like a drained vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is also as subtle as the delicate sheets.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not reach just to the bone, nor just to the nerve, and such disease is called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the doctor is required to cut around the entire wound, and similarly when it is subtle, just like one wraps.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not hesitate because of its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you find that the wounds are getting worse, and the decay is not on the surface,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the wound is full of flesh, so the treatment with a cluster follows:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Here is the translation:
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then the rectifier of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take arsenic, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put copper in a vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it into a liquid and into honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and clean the wound, and hold the peritons;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine sit for three hours, then strain it by pressing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the wounds are cicatrized, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and no time should be cleaned with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, it is that you take ashes of wood from vine, and throw water above.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then boil, and clarify, until you know that the blood is well purged;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot suffer it, nor the Egyptian medicine with water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if you clarify with water and honey or it has a little bit of littarge powder;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	where you apply a mixture of honey and wine, which has the properties of mundifying and cleaning,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the wounds are well cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if you apply a mixture of what creates birth to flesh in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take a definitive plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments, whose properties I have discussed in the treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the passage of the sinus is small, and the canal of theclyster cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you enlarge it with a iron instrument a little, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment,
