ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	where application of basilicon, so that it be enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, thus prick and let it suppurate as much as it can, or the cluster may enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the perforation that makes a hole is above, thus cover or make a lower level than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the hole is in the fontanelle, thus do not let it become inflamed there;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the seat below thus as you want,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it appears in such a manner that the bowel runs to the lowest place where it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bowel is perforated, if you do not allow it to become inflamed there
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the seat below thus as you want,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	if it appears in this manner: that the bowel moves gently downwards, and does not leave anything behind from the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and apply a dressing of linen that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cover the affected area of the breast, i.e. a small area larger than at first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then is the gentle adjustment of the bandage according to the quantity of the pierced hole.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the pierced hole of the breast to align the fracture, and do not remove the large bandage until after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is above the pierced hole of the breast, removes it frequently to reset the fracture,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know that which runs from the fracture, whether it is venom or poison or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when the medicine has extended in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps upon the tender part of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breasts are affected already, and approach the healthy ones;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then dislocate it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you dislocate the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	If you change the other dressing, and renew the binding.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the senses are disturbed by indigestion after many days, know that the senses are not yet clear.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle veins come to the surface after long tension, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For health approaches. For there are men who delay in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the bowel is indigestible, it knows how to release itself after many days, it seems that the breasts do not become accustomed;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are slow to heal, and are painful, if you apply moist medicines in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as we have said definitively, because it has a great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take ointment definitively, and make it with rose oil, and the juice of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	Then he must be cooked and used; and this same mixture makes honey-cooked groats.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when we apply it, it is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue it to the dressing, and apply it to the wound, and many times I have ministered to a logger's long wound,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the sky, which is as if flour of times and hundred.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in use of simples or of compounds: crush them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and in use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the treatment is prolonged, and it is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is in depth, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that grows beneath the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or at the foot, or which happens to grow on other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is inflamed, and one does not take care, if an abscess forms here,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and pour pus as far as it runs to the root of the finger, and by chance they corrupt everything;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there come ulcers up to the bone, as far as it comes to foul-smelling pain, and the head of the finger is swollen, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not profit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	Here is the translation:
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the flesh inside, and it starts to point, and becomes white,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must put something under the nail that points at the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and put the bottle up high, and hold this subtle and light character.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply to the remaining flesh of the wound medicines that are burning and corrosive to cauterize everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wounds thoroughly so that they heal.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cover it, and pull out strongly, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the finger decay, so cut it off at the joint as we said before that it is like that.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and swollen, and it feels great pain, so it is necessary that you heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut off the finger at the joint of the hand, cutting across the upper part;
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the incision does not reach just to the skin which is beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on it to calm it down.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain that comes from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two fingers that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all numb,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is a part where there are bones, and sometimes there is a fingernail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them grow from the root of the joint, or the birth is in no way from our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	That which grows on no nut of the toe does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and that which grows at the joint of the toe, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of the one who is fleshed is light, in such manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a large spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you hold two fingers together.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In those who are born with their fingers or toes bent inward, it is necessary that you first straighten the rounded flesh up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then feel the bone to a suitable socket, then heal it as long as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden movements that come together suddenly come from birth, or from a sudden wound, or from a burn by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it happens that you feel that dislocation, then the duty is to repair it according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or wrapped in a millstone oil rosset, so they do not dislocate;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	where you put between two subtle pieces of plank, so that the eyes are suspended, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	they suddenly come together with the palm, if they cope with that suspension as it is necessary.
Des vils	Of veins
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	They are large, swollen veins full of superfluous melancholic humors, which come into the limbs of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and there is more in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer sometimes purging of the colon, and then the juice of the basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron is according to two methods: one is that they cut, and treat on fire the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein, and treat it all on fire.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is done in this manner: first raise the leg to a warm and very hot temperature, so that the thick blood is subtitled.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then hold the leg of the patient from above the hip, just to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut into the vein in one, two, or three places, with a large incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then release and pull out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's vein can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the ligature, and he instructs that he abstains from eating meat cooked with black coal;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommend evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and do not annoy the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevations of the limb are in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and raise the leg to warm water as hot as it turns red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no balms, heat it with fire, and then apply the cup at the vein of the loin to the head of the knee, or in the part beneath the armpit;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the ankle, and strip the vein of each part, until it appears as one feels;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters under the skin it seems also like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the vein beneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then place it lightly at the ankle;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then burn with fire in another place, thus two wounds; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then apply the ointment to the wound, just as you have done, and attach it to another ulcer, just as you had done previously;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then burn with another cauterization, or more if you are a master of it, then apply the ointment, and burn on the toe of the foot;
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then remove and apply the ointment up to the second cauterization; then extract the cauterization from cauterization, until it is completely removed, then burn;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it back and lift it, if you prick with a strong double-threaded needle at all points.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and pull and tug, and prick below with a strong thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it is settled;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and take care that it does not seize up, for if it seizes up, you cannot pull or lift it, and harm comes to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have fully pulled it back, place on the wound a lint soaked in wine and rose oil; and treat until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if his vision is contracted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	it is necessary that you bend it gently, but do not touch it; and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron instrument with which one touches the vision is curved, and does not cut, so it does not touch the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of large curvature, for if it were subtle, it would touch the vein, but it is thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is in the legs, in warm regions where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in soil where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it grows in another part rather than the legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that comes from beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes from within the body, snakes and worms, growing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very large inflammation comes into the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then it changes the veins, and begins to swell outward, like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head opens, it is necessary that you envelop it with a piece of cloth seven and a half inches up to the elbow, and the nail,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth on the leg, and all the times it is not in default, if you envelop it with the cloth, and the nail;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut part of it off, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut into its root, until it is all removed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess and putrefaction in the limb, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and it is not at all times this vein when it is treated with five fingers' length, or ten inches;
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a hand came to me, whose fingers were ten inches long, and when you take its measure, if it bursts into four or five, and pierces just to the ends,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	Here is the translation:
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And often at this vein many times, and similarly when it opens into the joint of the foot, or where the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes from many perforations, and there are many ulcers; heal them thus as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From wounds that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land "ox disease", because it often affects the oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small vein that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the entire body, rising and falling,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it feels like a good flow from member to member, as much as it descends into the skin or it goes, and jumps forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is a sign of bad digestion of certain humors, if they come forth like worms and snakes and lice and ascarids or belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt not of its evil, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance returns, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it curving and straying, if one cannot be steadfast that when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	it is necessary then that you read the place above and below with a strong and well-straightened lien,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and the straying vein, and if the verse is deeply implanted in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If you cauterize with fire, until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that he does, is that he corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or approaching near the eye, hold the eyebrow firmly, then cope with it above, and remove it completely;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient's moderation of corpus of soluble medicines for the evil humidors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of rotten flesh eating away at the putridity.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes into some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from member to member; and I see what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it grow as big as a vein on the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more painful than anything, just like living silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little afterwards it corrupts throughout the whole body, so much that it comes into the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then it seems to me that it turns again inward towards the body, as I see it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised at how it moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen that many had wanted to move the pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not avoid what he wants, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, the constricted womb appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and I do not appear to be in accordance with this reason for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and recovered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you want to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, it appears as we have said.
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the lie is above and below hastily, and then cope with it until that windiness constrains the issue in its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure for those who expel windiness, such as foul-smelling pills, and pills of serpent's wisdom, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some which have large heads, and small ones, and notched, and rounded;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those which have jagged edges, and those which have lengths, and those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls on any member if it falls according to several manners: whether in a principal member it injures,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	if like brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then on any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you about afterwards, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many guises;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad symptom does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then extract it, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the symptom of the brain when the arrow is in the head and pierces the bone, and exits the forehead which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	it is when there is Scotomy and numbness and reversal and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and perplexity of understanding, and evacuations of the colon;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without force in the nostrils, or in the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and it jumps from the white moist wound appearing like a pimple, and it jumps out also as if bruised flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this is a sign that appears, if you hold back from the treatment, and extract the arrow so it does not remain inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls into the body are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not at all loose.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves as if it were a pimple, and in a dark bloody flux, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Here is the translation:
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that did not penetrate deeply into the arm is that without pus or swelling from the wound, and the throat is swollen, and the patient's color changes, and he sighs deeply and casts a high fever.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow head breaks into the covering of the bladder, it is beneath the small ribs; and it casts great anguish and great pain and sighs; and it moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow head breaks in the stomach, by chance it comes out of the wound with some undigested food.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow head breaks in the belly, and it comes out at a point of feces through the intestine, there is no hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the blood vessel breaks in the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as the arm and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the joint and the spine of the back and the ribs and the hips and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to several dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the blood vessel is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, thus I will tell you what happened to me, because I did something similar.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man whose blood vessel burst or broke in the root of the nail:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I touched it, and pulled from another part beneath the fat of the ear, and it was without feeling numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye beneath the skin beneath,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was put back, and could not be felt except for the tip towards the hollow,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and it was a large arrow of a Turkish bow, with an iron tip without any edge; the game was without harm, and no bad accidents happened to me.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And pull out a arrowhead from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrowhead at the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I seized the barbs, and subtly pulled as much as I could, and the Christian was saved.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrowhead from a man's body, which had fallen into his belly, and I thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then when it had passed thirty days, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and I engineered it, and I made the trajectory straight, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose arrow fell or stuck, and the wound is swollen above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and delay extracting the arrow from him, and do not disturb his natural disposition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you saw another man who had an arrow wound on his face, and the wound was swollen;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he lingered thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And they extracted an arrow from the king's prince's man, which was stuck in his nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was entirely removed.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the treatment after she had fallen, three days prior. If I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I touched her everywhere with a subtle touch, and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt a throbbing pain beneath her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the injured place a digestive attractive plaster, because the wounds do not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I appear to have healed the wound of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plaster daily, and restored the wounded place, and thus I held back the patient's long-term pain.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow, that is, a day within his nose; and it did not bother him.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicinal corroding medicine by gentle hours, until it was uncovered,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I touched, and felt the head of the arrow which had become stuck in the flesh;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I probed into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it went well beyond the terms for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then examine if the wound is where I touched the tendons, and the muscle of one part and another, and cannot issue;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to subtly feel and ingeniously examine the instruments, until I grasped it, that is, the well-made tendons.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, so that I may draw it, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror shows that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or I have told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your treatment on what I do not say, for the books cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters compare well a great many things, and on what is present and failing,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new work, and a new instrument, at the understanding of the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not issue from the limbs where they are fixed except in seven manners.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the skin where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps forth where it enters, it's an arrow entering into the flesh, and jumps forth at no time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if she does not jump now, let her wait until the flesh is porous within, and may the dislocation be alleviated.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if she is fixed in the bone, and she cannot exit, let her wait thus for some days, and move a little each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then she jumps, and if she does not jump, prick within at all .i. subtle forest, as much as the eyes within are enlarged, and then pull.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: if it does not trouble him, let it be until it is even afterwards for some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrowhead comes just to the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrowhead does not get fixed further than in the bone, and does not come just to the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains some days without a bad accident, if the engine of the wound is treated.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck in this way and cannot come out, if you apply tareres around, as I have told you; then heal the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded in the limb of the body so that one cannot see it, then seek it out with the entire tendon.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do so due to the narrowness of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow.
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or vein, if the wound is so large that the abscess is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow where it holds,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the flesh is torn which is deeply fixed with two fingers by the muscle where you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtly understand that you do not break the arrow, that you extract it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, if you leave it until the surrounding tissue is purified, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood counteracts you, if you diminish what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision into the nerve and vein, and make an effort so that you can extract the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	where you touch or press, or hold firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow fell on them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest aid that it can be, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens into something of it, or the skin is inflamed in a place if one sees or feels it outwardly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then upwards, as much as the tongs can grasp, and then extract: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly so that it enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then pulls it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then recommences the extraction until it comes forth;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a remainder of the arrowhead, cut around the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft breaks, and you want to administer a remedy, then it administers an instrument that cuts.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then apply force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is hairy, he applies it to the instrument with a point entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, then it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the veins are, so you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then heal the wound as it converges.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrowhead is in the hand or foot or belly or bladder or side, and it is near the surface, and you can touch it, then you can cover over it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of touching the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if that is necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to extract arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the blood.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the swelling vein is also like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to swell at the point of the blood, as if it were the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tendons to swell and to dry out, thus it is:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one bleeds are 21, because there it has or at the head 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	it is to know: 2 veins which are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech" veins;
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries which are in the 2 temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and those veins that are in the eyelids of the eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the nose-bridge;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the gums which are around the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are two in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the head, and the common people call it the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basiliac,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the artery is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the abdomen,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one that is bled, which appears clearly on the skin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little vein is the one that is between the auricular and anular, and if it has two roots;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and on the leg and where the feet are, there are three veins: one is below the curve of the hollow of the left shin.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second vein which is at the ankle of the right shin; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and on the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The knowledge of the veins that are behind the ears helps against ancient cataracts and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the healer, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and scrub the area where the veins are of a rough fabric; then the patient should restrain his neck to a single gaze,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	so that the veins appear behind the ears in the dependent areas of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	where the hammers strike your finger, and where you feel the pulsation beneath your finger, it is a sign of an abscess;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and thrust it beneath the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand to the entire vein above,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and peel back the skin well, you must give two drops of traversing, and make issue two bloods as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then hold it steady and raise it, until it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the arteries that are in the temples, if it is worth migrating to an old vein,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and swollen, and accustomed to opthalmia, and at the root of the watery eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the wound if it is thus as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient strains his neck, so much that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse beneath your finger, and then signs of the fracture;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then apply the cauterizing iron to the vein above your finger's tip, and insert the lancet below.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and apply the vein above, and the cope, as you have done with other veins, and make correction of the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then undo the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put it on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form the scar, and let it be until it is healthy; and we have already spoken of their coping and extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The illness of the forehead vein, which is just as valuable as the illness of the cephalic as ancient diseases of the face, and migraine, and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the illnesses constrict their neck by twisting, so much that the veins appear;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release to the patient the neck, and lay the vein so it is healthy and never swells from a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Here is the translation:
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	Here is the translation:
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting no ligament, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the vein, and let the vein be of equal traverse, a little thick, a little long, a little wide, for there is no cartilage.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they break; then make a correction of blood, as much as you have mastery, and then place it on the cushion, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein of the arm that is worth aagu, and to strong force, and to evil diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	As if migraine and redness come to the face, and especially when it is chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the blood is such that the patient contracts his neck, then stretches his nose to your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a subtle flame long, and hold it in the hollow of the eyebrow in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will now start to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too much in depth, and make a correction of the blood according to the necessity, then leave it for a night, because it is almost completely restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the .ij. joints helps with the straightening of the arm, and at the beginning of messelry, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and corroding, and herpes, and similar things;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the health is that the patients stretch their neck from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the masters stand above the patient's head, and the patients sit on a stool.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then prick the vein of the arm slightly larger, then draw out the blood moderately, as much as the master is;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then make another incision in the other vein, then release the ligature, and hold the veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and let it be until morning, so that the wound may be healthy.
De la sainie des leivres	About the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins above the liver helps with pain in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the liver, and painful nose and entrails.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the health is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck steady as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the liver, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right liver and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are recognized by this, that they are black, and by this, around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	examine one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you examine the largest of each part, and all thus make the veins that are above and below, for it is a similar manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the healthy area below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Here is the translation:
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the blood is such that the patient's blood is between your hands before the sun, and he raises his tongue, and looks from below on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	feel both the one and the other, and do not press too much in depth, for there are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck where one commonly feels are sensed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or when pricking everywhere, a large flame appears, or a subtle olive-green color if one cuts deeply, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the wideness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is useful for opening the veins that are full of gross blood apparent, and that contain gross blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for healing subtle veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the healer to heal carefully, and that he beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he touches the artery, and blood comes out, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not be pricking the phlegm, but rather trimming it like a nail.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the ulcer does not open manifestly, then you must extract it, and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	where you want no rupture of it, or you heal the vein in his arm: it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and trim the phlegm like a nail, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to examine the level of the wound, it is necessary that you stretch out the arm, that you touch the level as much as you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the level of the notch, and then stretch out the arm, and cover the vein of the flame with anise;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not strike into the artery when you see the level swollen, for it is of the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell up high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is not from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Here is the translation:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not cleansed, and it grows worse, and the medicine does not present itself to you, then cut open the artery so that it reveals the head of the veins; and cleanse the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a scraping of fistula, and make it, and take one of the embers and lay them well just next to the other journey;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound is cleansed, it's good; if not, then cure, as we have said, with powders that cleanse blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the cleansing remedies are not grievous in many dispositions for the small wound of the plague, and the possession of the doctrine of the arm's power.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein's wisdom is a thousand times better if it draws blood from above the head and below the body.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the vein to be warmed by the nerve that is below, and if it does not penetrate deeply enough, and it finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it becomes inflamed and the health is grievously affected, and by chance it cannot be healed;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and it is necessary to open the nerve many times, and if it does not open in any men because of its subtlety, it is necessary that you loosen the sinew of the instrument with ease; and avoid loosening the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then it should be made to flow gently.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sinew of the cephalic aids, which attracts blood from the head, and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to cauterize at the flame of olive oil or at the flame of mirtyne, because it is the safest of all the veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Here is the translation:
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance inflame the eyes of some men, when it fails at first, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about healing, is that healing is not achieved unless it preserves health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and it is the healthy vein made in one of the three veins that are or touched: that is to say, cephalic, fasting, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of spring, and in autumn, and in winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after 8 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for the illnesses has no determined hour, but only when need is felt by day or night, at all hours and in all tensions;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not advisable to cauterize children until 13 years old, nor a woman carrying fruit for four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor is it advisable to cauterize the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be cauterized, in whatever manner it may be, then it is advisable that they evacuate the intestines with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if it has much bad humors retained, then the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful humors from the intestines to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One does not become healthy who is too full of food, nor who is drunk, as long as he is furious, nor dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and becomes worse on the part of the sick one after colic passion, and vomiting, and discomfort of the stomach, and multiplication of habits in a woman, and of labor, of watching and of fasting, and all that is contrary to virtue, or by means of the arm or of the whole body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtle are the humors, if the blood is thick, through food and through drinks and through medicines, if you have them in great abundance;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then between or bath, it is not a thing that does not weaken, to subtily thin out the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and you close the vein of the foot below the thigh, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and you beware that day of operation, and of point, and of slipped disc, and of similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be gentle and joyful, and let the veins be higher than the one that is being treated, and rub the arm three or four times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligament above moderately, for when it is too stretched or short, it cannot correct the sinew;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then he rubs the joint with his hands until the veins swell, and he feels them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then he anoints the surgeons with a little oil of a small flask, then places his finger of his left hand under that vein below the joint where he wants to operate,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not flee and fails to be pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee as if they were cords to the surgeon, and if there are those that are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if one touches the flame, one draws back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, because it is necessary that the surgeons be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it's good; if not, then recommence a little below that place or in haste, if the vein is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the vein is swollen, and the patient is in spasm, let it be for a day or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Here is the translation:
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the perforation is small, or the bleeding is subtle and you doubt whether it has not bled as much as you see, then thrust the same perforation fully into the flame directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and hold it a little hastily, so that the eyes are inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the eyes inflamed, do not recommence the bleeding, and put a little of the oil of the lily on it, for it alleviates the body's pain of blood, and is modified in this eye with the oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the lily oil in each wound that you bleed, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same method makes a triangle and bulge of eyes, when one puts it on the place; if the blood is subtle and separates when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there come big abscesses, which occur many times, especially when it is not healthy enough except at that time when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hasten, and put on the place a sponge moistened with water and oil, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has issued from the vein, and if it remains on the place for several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put among none of those things of aloe or myrrh remedy in juice of calendula, masterly, or similarly.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is abscess and appearance at the healthy part of the basilica: put your hand on it then, and if you find the soft spot at the compression of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put on anything of those things that we have said, for by chance in court without the artery; but it makes .i. a plaster secure to harden the spot, then cure with another cure, until it be healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And extract each blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because the patient's blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see a large tumor, let it diminish until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and strong, and has mastery of blood extraction, that they make a larger wound, and let the flames be large.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him less often and more slowly, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking.
